Task interface - start/stop for individual tasks\n\nThe key insight from the code is the SERVICE STARTUP ORDERING in BrokerServer.startup():\n1. Scheduler startup\n2. Socket server setup\n3. lifecycle pattern with coordinated startup and shutdown sequences. The architecture follows the Startable/Stoppable pattern across multiple service components.\\n\\n## Core Lifecycle Pattern\\n\\nThe primary service lifecycle implementation is found in the KafkaRaftServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/KafkaRaftServer.scala), which manages both broker and controller components. In startup(), the controller starts first before the broker (lines 90-98), and in shutdown(), the broker shuts down first before the controller (lines 100-107). This ordering ensures that the controller remains available for broker shutdown operations.\\n\\n## Broker Service Lifecycle\\n\\nThe BrokerServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) implements the complex startup() method (line 189) that manages the initialization of numerous dependent services:\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Initialization** (line 204-205): The KafkaScheduler is created and started early to support all background tasks\\n2. **Socket Server Setup** (line 275-281): Network infrastructure initialization\\n3. **Metadata Cache Creation** (line 212): Core metadata caching\\n4. **Log Manager Initialization** (line 216-222): Log storage management\\n5. **Lifecycle Manager Creation** (line 224-228): Broker state tracking\\n6. **Coordinator Initialization** (lines 376-398): Group, share, and transaction coordinators\\n7. **Replica Manager Setup** (lines 345-364): Replication management\\n8. **Socket Server Enablement** (line 587): Final network activation\\n\\nThe shutdown() method (line 729) implements reverse dependency order:\\n1. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown/controlled shutdown (lines 735-753)\\n2. Socket server stops accepting requests (line 758)\\n3. Metadata publishers are removed (lines 760-761)\\n4. Request handlers shutdown (line 762-765)\\n5. **Scheduler shutdown EARLY** (line 778-779) - Critical to prevent concurrent access to closing resources\\n6. Coordinators shutdown in order: transaction, group, share (lines 781-789)\\n7. Replica manager shutdown (line 795)\\n8. Log manager shutdown (line 806-809)\\n9. Quota managers shutdown (line 815-816)\\n10. Socket server shutdown (line 818-819)\\n11. Lifecycle manager close (line 829-830)\\n\\nThis order is carefully designed to ensure that dependent services stop in reverse order of their startup, with the scheduler shutting down early to prevent background tasks from accessing resources being closed.\\n\\n## Scheduler Interface\\n\\nThe Scheduler interface (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java) defines the basic lifecycle contract with startup() and shutdown() methods, serving as a fundamental building block for all scheduled operations.\\n\\n## Coordinator Services\\n\\nBoth GroupCoordinator (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.java) and ShareCoordinator (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinator.java) implement startup(IntSupplier) and shutdown() methods, managing group and share coordination state respectively.\\n\\n## Kafka Connect Service Lifecycle\\n\\nThe Connect system implements a similar pattern with the Connect class (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java) managing the overall lifecycle. Start() initializes the herder and REST server (lines 70-71), while stop() reverses the order (lines 89-90), shutting down the REST server before the herder.\\n\\nThe Herder interface (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Herder.java) provides start/stop lifecycle methods for connector management.\\n\\nBacking stores implement the lifecycle pattern:\\n- ConfigBackingStore (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/ConfigBackingStore.java): Manages connector configurations\\n- StatusBackingStore (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/StatusBackingStore.java): Tracks connector/task status\\n- OffsetBackingStore (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/storage/OffsetBackingStore.java): Stores connector offsets\\n\\nEach implements start()/stop() methods to manage their initialization and cleanup.\\n\\n## Task Lifecycle\\n\\nThe Task interface (connect/api/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/connector/Task.java) provides start(Map<String, String>) and stop() methods for individual task lifecycle management.\\n\\n## Coordinated Shutdown in Test Infrastructure\\n\\nThe KafkaClusterTestKit (test-common/test-common-runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/test/KafkaClusterTestKit.java) demonstrates the coordinated startup and shutdown patterns. The startup() method (line 529) starts controllers first, then brokers in parallel. The close() method (line 695) follows the same pattern: brokers shutdown first (lines 700-706), then controllers (lines 708-714), ensuring proper dependency order.\\n\\n## Key Pattern Insights\\n\\n1. **Startup Order**: Dependencies are started in forward order (scheduler → log manager → coordinators)\\n2. **Shutdown Order**: Dependencies are stopped in reverse order to satisfy dependencies\\n3. **Early Scheduler Shutdown**: The scheduler shuts down early to prevent concurrent access to closing resources\\n4. **Coordinator Dependency Management**: Coordinators depend on the replica manager and other infrastructure\\n5. **Error Handling**: The CoreUtils.swallow() pattern allows graceful handling of shutdown errors without cascading failures\\n6. **Future-based Initialization**: Extensive use of CompletableFuture and FutureUtils.waitWithLogging ensures proper sequencing of async initialization steps\\n\\nThis comprehensive lifecycle pattern ensures that Apache Kafka services initialize and shutdown in a coordinated manner, respecting all dependencies and preventing race conditions or resource access violations.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3078,"cache_read_input_tokens":98388,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3078},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dafc6e26-aef3-4f3b-bb08-d5658844ce0b","uuid":"c77be452-e06c-4f5a-8be5-61730d2901e5"}

In startup(), the controller starts first before the broker (lines 90-98), and in shutdown(), the broker shuts down first before the controller (lines 100-107). This ordering ensures that the controller remains available for broker shutdown operations.\\n\\n## Broker Service Lifecycle\\n\\nThe BrokerServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) implements the complex startup() method (line 189) that manages the initialization of numerous dependent services:\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Initialization** (line 204-205): The KafkaScheduler is created and started early to support all background tasks\\n2. **Socket Server Setup** (line 275-281): Network infrastructure initialization\\n3. **Metadata Cache Creation** (line 212): Core metadata caching\\n4. **Log Manager Initialization** (line 216-222): Log storage management\\n5. **Lifecycle Manager Creation** (line 224-228): Broker state tracking\\n6. **Coordinator Initialization** (lines 376-398): Group, share, and transaction coordinators\\n7. **Replica Manager Setup** (lines 345-364): Replication management\\n8. **Socket Server Enablement** (line 587): Final network activation\\n\\nThe shutdown() method (line 729) implements reverse dependency order:\\n1. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown/controlled shutdown (lines 735-753)\\n2. Socket server stops accepting requests (line 758)\\n3. Metadata publishers are removed (lines 760-761)\\n4. Request handlers shutdown (line 762-765)\\n5. **Scheduler shutdown EARLY** (line 778-779) - Critical to prevent concurrent access to closing resources\\n6. Quota managers shutdown (line 815-816)\\n10. Socket server shutdown (line 818-819)\\n11.
